href="#cite_note-aenapax-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><br />Spanish <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a>, AENA<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b> Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport</b> (Spanish: <i lang="es">Aeropuerto Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez Madrid-Barajas</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ae\xc9\xbeo\xcb\x88pwe\xc9\xbeto a\xcb\x88\xc3\xb0olfo \xcb\x88swa\xc9\xbee\xce\xb8 ma\xcb\x88\xc3\xb0\xc9\xbei\xc3\xb0 \xce\xb2a\xcb\x88\xc9\xbeaxas]</a></span>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>MAD</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LEMD</b>), commonly known as <b>Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport</b>, is the main international airport serving <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> in Spain. At 3,050&#160;ha (7,500 acres) in area, it is the second-largest airport in Europe by physical size behind <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris\xe2\x80\x93Charles de Gaulle Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, 61.8&#160;million passengers travelled through Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas, making it the country\'s busiest airport as well as <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_Europe_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in Europe by passenger traffic">Europe\'s sixth-busiest</a>.\n</p><p>The airport opened in 1928 and has grown to be one of Europe\'s most important aviation centres. Within the city limits of Madrid, it is 9&#160;km (6&#160;mi) from the city\'s financial district and 13&#160;km (8&#160;mi) northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol" title="Puerta del Sol">Puerta del Sol</a> or <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Mayor,_Madrid" title="Plaza Mayor, Madrid">Plaza Mayor de Madrid</a>, Madrid\'s historic centre. The airport name derives from the adjacent district of <a href="/wiki/Barajas_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Barajas (district)">Barajas</a>, which has its own metro station on the same rail line serving the airport. Barajas serves as the gateway to the Iberian peninsula from the rest of Europe and the world and is a key link between Europe and Latin America. The airport is the primary hub and maintenance base for <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Airlines">Iberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a>. Consequently, Iberia is responsible for more than 40% of Barajas\' traffic. The airport has five passenger terminals: T1, T2, T3, T4 and T4S.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" and accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport was constructed in 1927, opening to national and international air traffic on 22 April 1931, although regular commercial operations began two years later. A small terminal was constructed with a capacity for 30,000 passengers a year, in addition to several hangars and the building of the Avi\xc3\xb3n Club. The first regular flight was established by <a href="/wiki/Lineas_A%C3%A9reas_Postales_Espa%C3%B1olas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lineas A\xc3\xa9reas Postales Espa\xc3\xb1olas">Lineas A\xc3\xa9reas Postales Espa\xc3\xb1olas</a> (LAPE) with its route to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. In the 1930s, flights started to serve some European and African destinations, the first international flights from the airport.\n</p><p>Originally, the flight field was a large circle bordered in white with the name of Madrid in its interior, unpaved, consisting of land covered with natural grass. It was not until the 1940s that the flight field was paved and new runways were designed. The first runway which started operation in 1944 was 1,400 metres long and 45 metres wide.<sup id="cite_ref-history_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the decade the airport had three runways, none of which exist today. In the late 1940s, scheduled flights to Latin America and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> started.\n</p><p>In the 1950s, the airport supported over half a million passengers, increasing to five runways and scheduled flights to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> began. The National Terminal, currently T2, began construction in 1954 and opened later that year. In the Plan of Airports of 1957, Barajas Airport is classified as a first-class international airport. By the 1970s, large jets were landing at Barajas, and the growth of traffic mainly as a result of tourism exceeded forecasts. At the beginning of the decade, the airport reached the 1.2&#160;million passengers, double that envisaged in the Plan of Airports of 1957.\n</p><p>In the 1970s, with the boom in tourism and the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>, the airport reached 4&#160;million passengers and began the construction of the international terminal (current T1). In 1974, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Airlines">Iberia</a>, L.A.E. introduced the shuttle service between Madrid and Barcelona, a service with multiple daily frequencies and available without prior reservation.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a> brought significant expansion and modernisation of the airport\'s two existing terminals.<sup id="cite_ref-history_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1990s, the airport expanded further. In 1994, the first cargo terminal was constructed and the control tower was renovated. In 1997, it opened the North Dock, which is used as an exclusive terminal for Iberia\'s <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen</a> flights. In 1998, it inaugurated a new control tower, 71 m tall and then in 1999 the new South Dock opened, which implies an expansion of the international terminal. During this time, the distribution of the terminals changed: The south dock and most of the International Terminal were now called T1, the rest of the International Terminal and Domestic Terminal were now called T2 and the north dock was called T3.\n</p><p>In November 1998, the new runway 18R-36L started operations (replacing the previous 18\xe2\x80\x9336), 4,400 m long, one of the largest in Europe under expansion plans called Major Barajas. In 2000, it began the construction of new terminals T4 and its satellite, T4S, designed by architects <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Lamela" title="Antonio Lamela">Antonio Lamela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rogers" title="Richard Rogers">Richard Rogers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Vidal" title="Luis Vidal">Luis Vidal</a>. Two parallel runways to the existing ones were also built.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_2000s">Development since the 2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development since the 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The new terminals and runways were completed in 2004, but administrative delays and equipment, as well as the controversy over the redeployment of terminals, delayed service until 5 February 2006.\n</p><p>Terminal 4, designed by Antonio Lamela, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rogers" title="Richard Rogers">Richard Rogers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Vidal" title="Luis Vidal">Luis Vidal</a>, (winning team of the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Prize" title="Stirling Prize">Stirling Prize</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Carillion" title="Carillion">TPS Engineers</a>, (winning team of the 2006 <a href="/wiki/IStructE_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="IStructE Awards">IStructE Award</a> for Commercial Structures)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> was built by <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">Ferrovial</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and inaugurated on 5 February 2006. Terminal 4 is one of the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">airport terminals</a> in terms of area, with 760,000 square meters (8,180,572 square feet) in separate landside and airside structures. It consists of a main building, T4 (470,000 m<sup>2</sup>) and a satellite building, T4S (290,000 m<sup>2</sup>), which are approximately 2.5&#160;km apart. The new Terminal 4 is designed to give passengers a stress-free start to their journey. This is managed through careful use of illumination, with glass panes instead of walls and numerous skylights which allow natural light into the structure. With this new addition, Barajas is designed to handle 70&#160;million passengers annually.\n</p><p>During the construction of Terminal 4, two more runways (15L/33R and 18L/36R) were constructed to aid in the flow of air traffic arriving and departing from Barajas. These runways were officially inaugurated on 5 February 2006 (together with the terminals), but had already been used on several occasions beforehand to test flight and air traffic manoeuvres. Thus, Barajas came to have four runways: two on a north\xe2\x80\x93south axis and parallel to each other (separated by 1.8&#160;km) and two on a northwest\xe2\x80\x93southeast axis (and separated by 2.5&#160;km). This allowed simultaneous takeoffs and landings into the airport, allowing 120 operations an hour (one takeoff or landing every 30 seconds).\n</p><p>Terminals 1, 2 and 3 are adjacent terminals that are home to <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> airlines. Terminal 4 is home to <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Airlines">Iberia</a>, its franchise <a href="/wiki/Air_Nostrum" title="Air Nostrum">Air Nostrum</a> and all <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> partner airlines. Gate numbers are continuous in terminals 1, 2 and 3 (A1 to E89), but are separately numbered in terminal 4 (H, J, K and M, R, S, U in satellite building).\n</p><p>The Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barcelona <a href="/wiki/Air_shuttle" title="Air shuttle">air shuttle</a> service, known as the "Puente A\xc3\xa9reo" (in Spanish), literally called "Air Bridge", used to be the busiest route between two EU airports<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> with 55 daily flights in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The schedule has been reduced since the February 2008 opening of the <a href="/wiki/Madrid%E2%80%93Barcelona_high-speed_rail_line" title="Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barcelona high-speed rail line">Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barcelona high-speed rail line</a> which covers the distance in <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math">2<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours. Subsequently, the route has been <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_passenger_air_routes" title="List of busiest passenger air routes">overtaken</a> by London-Dublin and Paris-Toulouse.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On the morning of 30 December 2006, an explosion took place in the carpark building module D attached to Terminal 4. Authorities received a <a href="/wiki/Bomb_threat" title="Bomb threat">bomb threat</a> at approximately 8:15 local time (7:15 <a href="/wiki/GMT" class="mw-redirect" title="GMT">GMT</a>), with the caller stating that a car bomb carried with 800&#160;kg of explosive would explode at 9:00 local time (8:00 GMT).<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_main_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters_main-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After receiving the warning, police were able to evacuate part of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Later, an anonymous caller stated that <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> claims responsibility for the bombing.<sup id="cite_ref-ETAClaim_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ETAClaim-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the explosion, two Ecuadorians who were sleeping in their cars died. The whole module D of the car park was levelled creating around 40,000 tonnes of debris. It took workers six days to recover the body of the second victim from the rubble.</li></ul>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport_bombing" title="2006 Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport bombing">2006 Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport bombing</a></div>\n<p>In 2007, the airport processed more than 52&#160;million passengers. Barajas was voted "Best Airport" in the 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast" title="Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast">Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast</a> Traveller Reader Awards</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2010, the Spanish government announced plans to tender Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas airport to companies in the private sector for a period of up to 40 years.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 January 2012, <a href="/wiki/Spanair" title="Spanair">Spanair</a> suspended all flights affecting Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas as well as other domestic and international connections.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 20 September 2012, both runways 15/33 were renamed as 14R/32L (the longest) and 14L/32R (the shortest).\n</p><p>On 1 August 2015, the first scheduled <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> flight landed in Madrid-Barajas in a daily service to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>.\n</p><p>Following the death of former Spanish Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez">Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez</a>, in 2014, the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Works_and_Transport_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Public Works and Transport (Spain)">Ministry of Public Works and Transport</a> announced<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> that the airport would be renamed <i>Aeropuerto Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez, Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas</i>. This renaming seeks recognition for Su\xc3\xa1rez\'s role as the first Prime Minister of Spain after the restoration of democracy and his key participation in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">transition to democracy</a> after the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>.\n</p><p>In late 2018 and early 2019, Iberia renovated its two lounges in Terminal 4, the Dali and Velazquez lounges.\n</p><p>In December 2019, the airport\'s operator <a href="/wiki/ENAIRE" title="ENAIRE">Aena</a> announced plans to significantly expand and renovate the existing installations, increasing their yearly capacity from 70 to 80&#160;million passengers and bridging the architectural gap between the original Terminals 1, 2 and 3 and the newer Terminal 4. The project has a budget of 750&#160;million Euro and is set to be executed in the period from 2022 to 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of April 2021, the following airlines serve 193 regular scheduled and charter routes to and from Madrid:<sup id="cite_ref-20" href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>\n</td>\n<td>806,692\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_care">Medical care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Medical care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The airport is attached to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal_University_Hospital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n y Cajal University Hospital (page does not exist)">Ram\xc3\xb3n y Cajal University Hospital</a> in Madrid as a reference hospital for medical and surgical emergencies requiring hospital care.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition, the airport itself has medical rooms and medical personnel attached to the Airport Medical Service to cover transit passengers who need medical attention.<sup id="cite_ref-aena.es_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aena.es-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> It also has 75 Cardiac Rescue Points equipped with defibrillators in the event of cardiorespiratory arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-aena.es_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aena.es-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All terminals have clearly signed <b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.madrid-airport.info/taxi-transfers.html">taxi ranks</a> outside the arrivals area</b>. <b>Official taxis</b> are white with a red stripe and have the Madrid City Council coat-of-arms on their doors.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Metro" title="Madrid Metro">Madrid Metro</a> Line connects the airport with city centre station <a href="/wiki/Nuevos_Ministerios_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuevos Ministerios Station">Nuevos Ministerios</a> in Madrid\'s financial district. The Barajas <b><a href="/wiki/Line_8_(Madrid_Metro)" title="Line 8 (Madrid Metro)">Line 8</a></b> provides a fast route from the underground stations at Terminal 2 (access to T1 and T3) and Terminal 4 into central Madrid. The metro also provides links to stations on the Spanish railway network.\n</p><p>In October 2006, a bid was launched for the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Cercan%C3%ADas_Madrid" title="Cercan\xc3\xadas Madrid">Cercan\xc3\xadas</a> link between <a href="/wiki/Chamart%C3%ADn_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamart\xc3\xadn Station">Chamart\xc3\xadn Station</a> and Terminal 4. Now finished, this single Cercan\xc3\xadas Line (C-1) links Madrid Barajas Terminal 4, with <a href="/wiki/Chamart%C3%ADn_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamart\xc3\xadn Station">Chamart\xc3\xadn Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Atocha_railway_station" title="Madrid Atocha railway station">Atocha</a> AVE high-speed train stations.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011 a decision was made to equip this link with <a href="/wiki/Dual_gauge" title="Dual gauge">dual gauge</a> which will allow <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE high-speed trains</a> to reach the airport station.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuevos_Ministerios_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuevos Ministerios Station">Nuevos Ministerios</a> metro station opened a satellite check-in center in 2002<sup id="cite_ref-V\xc3\xada_Libre_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V\xc3\xada_Libre-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> right by the <a href="/wiki/AZCA" title="AZCA">AZCA</a> business area in central Madrid; the satellite check-in center was permanently closed in 2006 due to security concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_SEPLA_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_SEPLA-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Bus">Metropolitan Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EMT (<a href="/wiki/Empresa_Municipal_de_Transportes_de_Madrid" title="Empresa Municipal de Transportes de Madrid">Madrid Municipal Transport Company</a>) runs regular public bus services between the airport and Madrid (Avenida de Am\xc3\xa9rica station): bus 200 runs as a complete line \xe2\x80\x93 dropping passengers at departures of terminals 1, 2 and 4 before collecting passengers in the reverse order at arrivals. The EMT public night bus service N4 (nicknamed "Buho", Owl) also services from Madrid downtown (Plaza Cibeles) to Barajas (Plaza de los Hermanos Falc\xc3\xb3 y Alvarez de Toledo, 400m from the airport through a passageway above the highway). EMT also have an express bus linking Barajas airport to Renfe\'s <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Atocha_railway_station" title="Madrid Atocha railway station">Atocha Station</a>, the main rail station in Madrid, during day and Plaza Cibeles during night. Unlike the two services mentioned above, this line runs 24 hours of the day during all the days of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>CRTM (<a href="/wiki/Consorcio_Regional_de_Transportes_de_Madrid" title="Consorcio Regional de Transportes de Madrid">Consorcio Regional de Transportes de Madrid</a>) runs four bus services between the airport and nearby cities in the metropolitan area:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>822</b>: T1 - <a href="/wiki/Coslada" title="Coslada">Coslada</a> - <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando_de_Henares" title="San Fernando de Henares">San Fernando de Henares</a></li>\n<li><b>824</b>: T2 - <a href="/wiki/Torrej%C3%B3n_de_Ardoz" title="Torrej\xc3\xb3n de Ardoz">Torrej\xc3\xb3n de Ardoz</a> - <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcal\xc3\xa1 de Henares">Alcal\xc3\xa1 de Henares</a></li>\n<li><b>827</b>: Canillejas - T4 - <a href="/wiki/Alcobendas" title="Alcobendas">Alcobendas</a> - <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_de_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Aut\xc3\xb3noma de Madrid">Universidad Aut\xc3\xb3noma de Madrid</a> - <a href="/wiki/Tres_Cantos" title="Tres Cantos">Tres Cantos</a></li>\n<li><b>828</b>: Canillejas - T4 - <a href="/wiki/Alcobendas" title="Alcobendas">Alcobendas</a> - <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_de_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Aut\xc3\xb3noma de Madrid">Universidad Aut\xc3\xb3noma de Madrid</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Long_distance_coaches">Long distance coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Long distance coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From terminals T1 and T4 the bus company Avanzabus operates routes to <a href="/wiki/%C3%81vila,_Spain" title="\xc3\x81vila, Spain">\xc3\x81vila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castell%C3%B3n_de_la_Plana" title="Castell\xc3\xb3n de la Plana">Castell\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">Salamanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> y <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">Zamora</a>. From terminal T4 the Alsa bus company runs services to the cities of <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Spain" title="Le\xc3\xb3n, Spain">Le\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">Murcia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gij\xc3\xb3n">Gij\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lugo" title="Lugo">Lugo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coru%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Coru\xc3\xb1a">Coru\xc3\xb1a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela" title="Santiago de Compostela">Santiago de Compostela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burgos" title="Burgos">Burgos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Spain" title="Santander, Spain">Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logro%C3%B1o" title="Logro\xc3\xb1o">Logro\xc3\xb1o</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>. From terminal T1 the Socibus company runs services to the major cities in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">Huelva</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C\xc3\xb3rdoba, Spain">C\xc3\xb3rdoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadiz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadiz">Cadiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerez" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerez">Jerez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_People_Mover">Airport People Mover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airport People Mover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Barajas_Airport_People_Mover" title="Madrid Barajas Airport People Mover">Madrid Barajas Airport People Mover</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:APM_Madrid_airport.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/APM_Madrid_airport.JPG/220px-APM_Madrid_airport.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/APM_Madrid_airport.JPG/330px-APM_Madrid_airport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/APM_Madrid_airport.JPG/440px-APM_Madrid_airport.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:APM_Madrid_airport.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Automated People Mover that links Terminal 4 and the Terminal 4 Satellite</div></div></div>\n<p>In early 2006, the first driverless transit system in Spain and the longest airport people mover system in Europe began transporting passengers between the new terminal (T4) and a new satellite terminal (T4S). Deploying the CITYFLO 550 automatic train control technology, the system is the only mode of transportation for passengers between the two terminals, which are spaced more than two kilometres apart.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Bombardier became the only contractor for the completely underground shuttle system, including the construction of the civil works, operation and maintenance of the system.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_parking">Airport parking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Airport parking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Long- and short-term car parking is provided at the airport with seven public parking areas. P1 is an outdoor car park located in front of the terminal building; P2 is an indoor car park with direct access to terminals T2 and T3. A Parking \'Express\' facility, available for short periods only, is located at Terminal 2 and dedicated long-term parking is also available with 1,655 spaces; a free shuttle operates between the long-stay car park and all terminals. There are also VIP car parks.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 30 September 1972, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-47" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas C-47">Douglas C-47</a>B EC-AQE of <a href="/wiki/Spantax" title="Spantax">Spantax</a> crashed on take-off. The aircraft was being used for training duties and the student pilot over-rotated and stalled. One of the six people on board was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN300972_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN300972-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 27 November 1983, <a href="/wiki/Avianca_Flight_011" title="Avianca Flight 011">Avianca Flight 011</a> crashed while attempting to land. Flight 011 struck a series of hills, causing the plane\'s right wing to break off. The 747 then cartwheeled, shattering into five pieces before coming to rest upside-down. Only 11 of the 169 passengers survived \xe2\x80\x93 there were no survivors among the 23 crew.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 7 December 1983, an Iberia 727 operating as <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Flight_350" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Flight 350">Iberia Flight 350</a><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> collided during takeoff with <a href="/wiki/Aviaco_Flight_134" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviaco Flight 134">Aviaco Flight 134</a>, a DC-9<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The Aviaco DC-9 had accidentally entered the runway as the Iberia flight was taking off.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Ninety-three people were killed, including 51 from the Iberia 727 and 42 from the Aviaco DC-9.</li>\n<li>On 15 July 2006, the winglet of a <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Thai Airways International">Thai Airways International</a> Boeing 747-400 HS-TGY operating flight TG943 from Madrid Barajas Airport in Spain to Rome Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport cut off the tail of an Air France ERJ-145 while taxiing to the runway for take-off. No injuries were reported.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 20 August 2008, <a href="/wiki/Spanair_Flight_5022" title="Spanair Flight 5022">Spanair Flight 5022</a> which was travelling to Gran Canaria, veered off to the right and into the ground while climbing immediately after lifting off from runway 36L at 14:45 local time. The <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-82" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-82">McDonnell Douglas MD-82</a> with registration "EC-HFP", was carrying 172 people, including 162 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In the accident, 154 people were killed, two were seriously injured and 12 were slightly injured. Prime Minister Zapatero ordered three days of national mourning.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
